  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d3d5426d-1605-4bdd-bea4-2d75b22e1f2e'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2278081124804574953">With epic sweep and breathtaking adventure, Sara Donati’s bestselling saga of an Early American family’s struggle for survival in the Northeast wilderness continues with the story of an indomitable woman and an unforgettable journey of redemption across a young nation threatened by the flames of war.<br/><br/>The year is 1812 and Hannah Bonner has returned to her family’s mountain c</span>
  <span id="freeText2278081124804574953" style="display:none">With epic sweep and breathtaking adventure, Sara Donati’s bestselling saga of an Early American family’s struggle for survival in the Northeast wilderness continues with the story of an indomitable woman and an unforgettable journey of redemption across a young nation threatened by the flames of war.<br /><br />The year is 1812 and Hannah Bonner has returned to her family’s mountain cabin in Paradise. But Nathaniel and Elizabeth Bonner can see that Hannah is not the same woman as when she left. For their daughter has come home without her husband and without her son…and with a story of loss and tragedy that she can’t bear to tell. Yet as Hannah resumes her duties as a gifted healer among the sick and needy, she finds that she is also slowly healing herself. Little does she realize that she is about to be called away to face her greatest challenge ever.<br /><br />As autumn approaches, news of the latest conflict with Britain finds the young men of Paradise—including eighteen-year-old Daniel Bonner—eager to take up arms. Against their better judgment, Nathaniel and Elizabeth must let him go, just as they must let his twin sister Lily, a stubborn beauty, pursue her independence in Montreal. But on the eve of the War of 1812, an unexpected guest arrives from Scotland: It is the Bonners’ distant cousin, the newly widowed Jennet Scott of Carryckcastle. Far from home, Lily and Jennet will each learn the price of pursuing their dreams and the possibility of true love.<br /><br />But it’s Hannah herself who must risk everything once more—this time to save Daniel, who’s been taken prisoner by the British. As the distant thunder of war threatens Paradise, Hannah may learn to live—and maybe love—again in one final act of courage, duty, and sacrifice.<br /><br />A gifted writer, a master storyteller, and a first-rate historian, Sara Donati has written a powerful, poignant, and movingly romantic novel that chronicles the lives and adventures of a family as compelling and unforgettable as any in American fiction.<br /><br /><br /><i>From the Hardcover edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2278081124804574953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1507987-i-am-tired-of-reading-about-jemima-kuick">I am tired of reading about Jemima Kuick. This the fourth in a series of novels containing noble, complicated people in a beautiful setting. Why the sudden plunge into a nasty soup called Jemima Kuick? I&#39;m plodding through the smarmy details of Jemima&#39;s trial. Suddenly, a biography about Winston Churchill looks very good.</a>
</div>

<div id="review_436384411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436384411" />
    <a title="Gail Amendt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5739689-gail-amendt"><img alt="Gail Amendt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443991099p2/5739689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436384411?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gail Amendt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail Amendt" href="/user/show/5739689-gail-amendt">Gail Amendt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436384411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17839870247195032682">After a bit of a hiccup with the third book, this series is back on track with the fourth. Set ten years after the last book, we find the Bonner children grown, Hannah returned from the west having lost her husband and son, and the family being caught up in the War of 1812. We see small snippets of the war as it played out along the border between New York and Quebec, but never the big picture, and while for me that is a little frustrating, I also appreciate that it is exactly the way war is exp</span>
  <span id="freeText17839870247195032682" style="display:none">After a bit of a hiccup with the third book, this series is back on track with the fourth. Set ten years after the last book, we find the Bonner children grown, Hannah returned from the west having lost her husband and son, and the family being caught up in the War of 1812. We see small snippets of the war as it played out along the border between New York and Quebec, but never the big picture, and while for me that is a little frustrating, I also appreciate that it is exactly the way war is experienced by those involved, only seeing a small part of a very big picture. As a Canadian, I found reading about the War of 1812 from an American perspective a little strange and very interesting. It's certainly not what we were taught at school, not that the War of 1812 gets much attention at school.<br /><br />Of course, with this series there is always romance, this time involving Elizabeth and Nathaniel's daughter Lily, and unlike the last book it is a real romance, not the rushed afterthought at the end of the book that saw Hannah marrying and leaving for the west. I have to say Lily is not my favorite character, but she did grow on me. <br /><br />My one complaint about this one is that I think there should have been another book between this one and the previous one. Ten years has passed, during which Hannah was living with an Indian husband in the west, during a period of much conflict between the Indians and settlers. While Hannah does not talk much about the traumatic events that led her to return to her family, we do learn that her husband fought with Tecumseh. This was a fascinating period in American history, and would have made a great book. I can only hope that Sara Donati will decide to address these missing years in a future book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17839870247195032682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14643237711109036894">I am completely enjoying this series. The thing I liked the most is that these books pull me in and they become a bit of an escape for me (which I'm needing this summer). I wish I had more to read to get me through the next week or two.   <span id="freeText14643237711109036894" style="display:none">I am completely enjoying this series. The thing I liked the most is that these books pull me in and they become a bit of an escape for me (which I'm needing this summer). I wish I had more to read to get me through the next week or two. I love this kind of historical fiction. It covers multi generations. It also has great characters and a great historical background.<br /><br />The characters from previous books were evolving in this book (the 4th in the series) and there were some new characters introduced that were kind of quirky. Hannah is the only one, we don't really learn anything new about as she flounders from some unknown trauma....I hope the next book addresses that. The romance didn't even bother me. There were plenty of other things going on which was appreciated. There was also more adventure in this one than the last one I read. That is always a plus for me. <br /><br />The books in this series are kind of long, but they don't feel long. I noticed more of the writing of the author in this one then in subsequent reads. I love her way with words. I thought on more than one occasion, "Beautiful."</span>

<div id="review_234405653" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234405653" />
    <a title="Dorine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6942470-dorine"><img alt="Dorine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384927238p2/6942470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234405653?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorine" href="/user/show/6942470-dorine">Dorine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36686371-fire-along-the-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=print-tbr">print-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=tzq">tzq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=family-dynamics">family-dynamics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=fiction-with-romance-elements">fiction-with-romance-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=for-nature-lovers">for-nature-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=1800s">1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=colonial-america">colonial-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942470-dorine?shelf=warrior">warrior</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234405653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5931911712137101269">FIRE ALONG THE SKY by Sara Donati is Book 4 in one of my favorite American Frontier historical series. I like this series so much that even though I have a print copy of this book, when the digital version went on sale I had no qualms about downloading it too. Book 4 did not disappoint, even if it has been awhile since I read the previous books. Luckily, Sara Donati is kind to her readers and includes a complete character list, so it’s easy to jog our memories.<br/><br/><b>Why this cover for the Cover Girl c</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5931911712137101269" style="display:none">FIRE ALONG THE SKY by Sara Donati is Book 4 in one of my favorite American Frontier historical series. I like this series so much that even though I have a print copy of this book, when the digital version went on sale I had no qualms about downloading it too. Book 4 did not disappoint, even if it has been awhile since I read the previous books. Luckily, Sara Donati is kind to her readers and includes a complete character list, so it’s easy to jog our memories.<br /><br /><b>Why this cover for the Cover Girl challenge?</b> I must admit to being a cover loving fool. I buy books just because I love their cover. It all stems from my commercial art training in high school in an accelerated vocational program prior to the digital art of today. Color is especially appealing to me, and who can resist a sunset? But, this wasn’t the only beautiful cover begging to be read in my TBR Mountain Range. Two things made me choose this book. That gorgeous font in the title, as well as loving all the previous books in the Wilderness series.<br /><br />Just to prove how much I love buying books by their covers, these are the books I had set aside for this challenge when FIRE ALONG THE SKY won my favor. <a href="http://thezestquest.com/2018/11/21/review-fire-along-the-sky-by-sara-donati/" rel="nofollow noopener">(see the covers here on my site)</a> Can anyone see a trend here?<br /><br />Yes, I’m a bit obsessed with Westerns or Frontier Historicals as well as modern day Westerns.<br /><br />As an avid fan of this series, I can’t imagine reading the books without a character list of some sort. There is an enormous amount of characters, some with similar names, and it doesn’t take much to get me confused. The books are so big that I rarely reread them prior to starting the next one in my pile. That said, I have read the first book, INTO THE WILDERNESS, several times.<br /><br />Elizabeth and Nathaniel Bonner are my favorite couple, so I’m especially pleased that their story continues in each book. FIRE ALONG THE SKY is no different. Although, I was especially intrigued by Hannah, Woman Walks Ahead, and her sister Lily. Those of you who have been reading my reviews for a while will remember that I reviewed <a href="http://thezestquest.com/2012/04/27/review-lake-in-the-clouds-by-sara-donati/" rel="nofollow noopener">LAKE IN THE CLOUDS</a> in 2012. It has taken me six years to get back to this series. For shame, because the entire time I was reading FIRE ALONG THE SKY, I wondered what had taken me so long to get back to them. Maybe I can finish this series by next year? I surely want to! And to be honest, I would love to find the time to begin with the first book and read the entire series back-to-back all over again.<br /><br />There’s so much to love in this book. Revisiting with favorite characters and tracking their progress in life is especially rewarding, heartrending, laugh-out loud funny, and downright scary. I never know where Sara Donati will lead us, and she doesn’t shy away from tragedy any more than a lifetime romance. She tortures her characters and her readers right along with them, and I can’t get enough of it, including the heartache.<br /><br />The writing is beautiful with lush descriptions in the right places that give these books an otherworldly feel. Don’t worry — the lush writing doesn’t overwhelm because the dialog and thoughts move along at a good clip as well. FIRE ALONG THE SKY concentrates on Lily quite a bit, which I loved because she’s an artist. It makes me wonder if Sara Donati is an illustrator as well as a polished wordsmith. Her descriptions of Lily’s talent is spot-on, as if it’s written from an experienced artist’s point-of-view. As you can see – this book contains many of my favorite themes: Scottish men in early America, artists, frontier living, mystery/thriller sections, backwoods details, the harsh reality of Native American’s history, as well as several love stories.<br /><br />Sara Donati writes an absorbing tale with characters who bound from the pages like old friends. I laughed out loud at the letters from the family at Lake in the Clouds, written to Lily who was visiting her brother Luke in Canada. Then, I gasped in horror at what happened next. This book has a good murder mystery to add to its attributes, which brings all the characters back together as it’s resolved.<br /><br />I bit off more than I can chew by selecting this 655 page book for our challenge just a week before it was due, but I couldn’t resist it. I’ve written this review based on reading 44% of it because I wanted to share all the books I discovered in my TBR while deciding on this one. Now I have a reading list planned for winter, including the rest of this series. I’ll come back to this review and write my final thoughts at the end of the book, but so far, I’m loving it.<br /><br />If you haven’t tried this series yet, I highly suggest you begin with INTO THE WILDERNESS and see if you love it as much as I do. I’d love to hear your thoughts if you do.<br /><br /><b>Final thoughts on November 24, 2018 when I finished the book</b> – Once again I’m frustrated that the story has unanswered questions that make me frenzied, but I’m equally excited to read the next book. I was a little disappointed that one evil preacher and his nephew’s stories were not enough closure for me. But that’s one molecule of disappointment in comparison to the exaggeration of enjoyment these books bring me.<br /><br />This series is a great American classic and shouldn’t be missed by historical fiction lovers. Next to Diana Gabaldon, Donati exceeds for me because she writes about the American frontier. Otherwise, I feel they’re equal in so many ways. Sara Donati delivers epic storytelling at its finest.<br /><br /><b>Review by Dorine, courtesy of <a href="http://thezestquest.com/2018/11/21/review-fire-along-the-sky-by-sara-donati/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Zest Quest</a>. Print and digital copies of this book, as well as the rest of the series have been purchased.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5931911712137101269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_233328771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233328771" />
    <a title="Melodie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5788507-melodie"><img alt="Melodie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579040834p2/5788507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233328771?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melodie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melodie" href="/user/show/5788507-melodie">Melodie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5788507-melodie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233328771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12823462609717494085"> Book 4 in the Wilderness series picks up the Bonners ten years after Hannah's marriage and departure from the family nest. It chronicles her journey back to the family having lost her husband and son. I found this to be jarring and a big disappointment. However throughout the course of the book the holes in her marital history are filled in somewhat, but not to my satisfaction.<br/> The rest of the Bonners and their relationships with the citizens of Paradise are given a lot of ink and I was glad of</span>
  <span id="freeText12823462609717494085" style="display:none"> Book 4 in the Wilderness series picks up the Bonners ten years after Hannah's marriage and departure from the family nest. It chronicles her journey back to the family having lost her husband and son. I found this to be jarring and a big disappointment. However throughout the course of the book the holes in her marital history are filled in somewhat, but not to my satisfaction.<br /> The rest of the Bonners and their relationships with the citizens of Paradise are given a lot of ink and I was glad of that. Where and who they live with and around has always fascinated me.Cousin Jennet comes across the pond from Scotland to live with the Bonners. Lily, the youngest daughter and most like her mother in temperament deals with her heart's growing pains as she tries to decide between two men. <br /> The last quarter of the book for the most part is devoted to the rescue mission undertaken by Hannah and Jennet to free her brother Daniel. The War of 1812 is dealt with in short bursts, but background is missing for the most part. But it prompted me to do a little research to educate myself, which is one of the reasons I love historical fiction.<br /> The premise of book five is set up with Jennet's kidnapping. I can only hope that Ms. Donati sees fit to fill in the familial holes that she left open.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12823462609717494085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4242767334684146075" style="display:none"><i>Ok, after the last book in the series I was sure that I wouldn't read another one... I was wrong.</i> Somehow "Fire" found it's way into my shopping bag after a brief trip to the local BAM. <br /><br />I was so happy that Donati didn't kill off Curiosity Freeman but was shocked that Dr. Richard Todd met an early and quite painful demise. Hannah's husband (who just appears out of nowhere in "Lake in the Clouds") never really materlizes in "Fire." His story was poorly told and their marriage was a complete waste of good paper. I couldn't even muster any realy sympathy for the death of Hannah's son.<br /><br />Donati introduced some quirky characters (Rev. Stiles and his nutcase of a nephew for instance)a hot new Scottish love interest and one heck of an adventure in a military prison. The story ends with a disjointed cliffhanger (Jennet should be throttled for leaving those letters in her tent. <b>What a bloody idiot!</b>)Taken altogether "Fire in the Sky" offered just enough to earn three stars. <br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText9870224549196001027" style="display:none">I started this series nearly 5 years ago-read the first three and then was never able to find the next 3. I forgot all about it. Thanks to a challenge I was doing I discovered this one my shelf.<br /><br />This is the saga of the Bonner Family, living on a mountain near the village of Paradise, in up state New York. The story, in book 1, begins in 1792. In Book 4 we are in the year 1812 and war has returned. The children are all grown and scattering and a cousin from Scotland arrives unexpectedly. I was afraid that I would be lost, as it took so long for me to return to this series. Surprisingly. I was able to recall quite a bit from the previous books. I suppose that is, in part, due to Donati's wonderful writing. She pulled me right back into the lives of all these wonderful characters.<br /><br />Looks like Michigan is headed for total lock-down again and I am looking forward to escaping into the Bonner family's world with books 5 and 6.<br /><br />Highly recommend the series to anyone who loves HF and great family saga.</span>

<div id="review_143785819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143785819" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877728-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579291918p2/4877728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143785819?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/4877728-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877728-melissa?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877728-melissa?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143785819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11495649915520212681">I couldn't bring myself to like this novel as much as the others in the series. As a bit of a recap, the series starts out with Elizabeth coming to America from England to be a school teacher. A self professed spinster, she is surprised when she falls in love with outdoors-man Nathaniel Bonner. She elopes with him in an effort to not only be with him forever, but also restore property rightfully to the people who own it. The next novel is a bit down the road and she has just given birth to twins</span>
  <span id="freeText11495649915520212681" style="display:none">I couldn't bring myself to like this novel as much as the others in the series. As a bit of a recap, the series starts out with Elizabeth coming to America from England to be a school teacher. A self professed spinster, she is surprised when she falls in love with outdoors-man Nathaniel Bonner. She elopes with him in an effort to not only be with him forever, but also restore property rightfully to the people who own it. The next novel is a bit down the road and she has just given birth to twins. They are kidnapped and Nathaniel and Elizabeth must travel to Scotland to get them back. From here we journey back to America many years down the road. This story is more about Nathaniel's daughter from his first wife and her learning to be a doctor despite her mixed heritage and the fact that she is a woman.<br /><br />Finally in this novel yet another great many years have passed. Hannah has come back after losing both her child and her husband. Lost in spirit she only lives day to day in repitition. Lily, one of the twins is dealing with her own love life and whether she loves the dashing Scot Simon or the married man in town. She decides to go to Canada to study art for awhile and get away from everything. Meanwhile, her twin Daniel has gone off to join the war and fight. In doing so, he is captured and injured. Hannah and their cousin from Scotland, Jennet sneak in as nursemaids to help care for him and hopefully rescue him. There are some suspicious of them however, so they must tread carefully if they have hopes of saving him and the other prisoners.<br /><br />My biggest complaint about this book would be the lack of writing about Nathaniel and Elizabeth. This was originally their story and it seems like they have become merely background characters in it. Also, the characters I did care about, like Hannah are not themselves. Granted she goes through a traumatic experience in this book but there was not as much depth to her character as in previous books. The characters the book did focus on, Jennet and Lily, weren't really characters I cared too much about. I would have rather heard more on the characters I was attached to already.<br /><br />As far as plot goes for this book, it had some interesting ideas but I don't think they were well carried out. What happened in the novel should have been exciting, but instead dragged out rather slowly. I lost interest several times and caught myself skimming the endless "letters" included in the novel.<br /><br />On another note, I do always enjoy Donati's writing style. Her background as a linguist makes the accents interesting and fairly realistic. She also includes description, but not too much that you tire of reading the book. While she does allude to some risque things in her book, they are not heavily described so even more timid readers can enjoy the book.<br /><br />I'll continue reading the story of course, but I hope Donati goes back to what drew me to the story in the first place. She has a great set of original characters, and she should use them to her advantage.<br /><br />Fire Along the Sky<br />Copyright 2004<br />608 pages </span>
  <a data-text-id="11495649915520212681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3174819303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3174819303" />
    <a title="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm"><img alt="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555952303p2/5289134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3174819303?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" href="/user/show/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm">Laurie • The Baking Bookworm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/46027444-fire-along-the-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm?shelf=reading-again">reading-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3174819303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer246232860161125955">The Into the Wilderness series has been one of my favourite historical fiction series to date. I read the series years ago and recently I've been working my way through listening to the books. Unfortunately, this time I wasn't as enamored with the Bonner clan. The things I loved about the books (the Bonner family - particularly Nathaniel and Elizabeth, the adventure and antics of the local people of Paradise, NY) felt very subdued and not all that interesting making the story drag throughout the</span>
  <span id="freeText246232860161125955" style="display:none">The Into the Wilderness series has been one of my favourite historical fiction series to date. I read the series years ago and recently I've been working my way through listening to the books. Unfortunately, this time I wasn't as enamored with the Bonner clan. The things I loved about the books (the Bonner family - particularly Nathaniel and Elizabeth, the adventure and antics of the local people of Paradise, NY) felt very subdued and not all that interesting making the story drag throughout the middle. <br /><br />My lackluster feelings are mainly from the fact that Fire Along The Sky picks up a decade after the last book, Lake in the Clouds. This jump in time forces Donati to tell her readers what has happened instead of showing them through the story. This time jump removed me from the story and affected my connection to the characters. Twins Lily and Daniel were 8 years old the last we saw them and now they're 18, and much of this book now focuses on Lily. She's not my favourite character and often came off as petulant rather than strong. I was excited to see that Hannah makes her return to Paradise, but she is kept in the background and is a shadow of her former self while my favourites, Nathaniel and Elizabeth, are kept squarely in the background. <br /><br />I'm saddened that I didn't love this book as much as I did previously. It felt like there were a lot of minor story lines to keep readers busy, but they didn't add a lot to the plot leaving this book to feel like just a link between the third and fifth books in the series. Even though I remember loving the fifth and sixth books, Queen of Swords and The Endless Forest , I'm debating whether to stop listening to this series. While Kate Reading as narrator continues to do an amazing job telling the story, it's the story itself that has lost some of its magic for me this second time around.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10858297656233609819" style="display:none">This is the 4th book o the Wilderness Series.<br /><br />Hannah Bonner has returned home to her family on Lake in the Clouds. <div id="review_488686853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488686853" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9636441-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546443259p2/9636441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488686853?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/9636441-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9636441-katie?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9636441-katie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488686853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5661912140557002442">When I first picked up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72854.Into_the_Wilderness__Wilderness___1_' title='Into the Wilderness (Wilderness, #1) by Sara Donati' rel='nofollow noopener'>Into the Wilderness</a> and started reading I nearly died of happiness to see the characters from one of my favorite movies (The Last of the Mohicans) in it!!!!The first three books were wonderful and fabulously written. Watching Elizabeth and Nathaniel's relationship grow and their children was an absolute pleasure. I did have some hesitations at first with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_' title='Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lake in the Clouds</a>, but Donati's style and writing cleared up some of the earlier hesitations I had. <br/><br/>Now onto Fire Along</span>
  <span id="freeText5661912140557002442" style="display:none">When I first picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72854.Into_the_Wilderness__Wilderness___1_" title="Into the Wilderness (Wilderness, #1) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Into the Wilderness</a> and started reading I nearly died of happiness to see the characters from one of my favorite movies (The Last of the Mohicans) in it!!!!The first three books were wonderful and fabulously written. Watching Elizabeth and Nathaniel's relationship grow and their children was an absolute pleasure. I did have some hesitations at first with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a>, but Donati's style and writing cleared up some of the earlier hesitations I had. <br /><br />Now onto Fire Along the Sky. I think this could have been a fabulous book, a wonderful book....if not for a two nagging and annoying lingering doubts and blanks Donati left. First...the jump in time. I understand you can't have books falling year after year after year, but it really was a drastic jump. One minute I'm reading about the 8 year old twins and a newly married Hannah, and the next minute (well not really the next minute more like the next week)I'm reading about 18 year old twins who are leaving Paradise and a shell of the former Hannah who Donati just tells us has been presumably widowed and lost her only child. That leads me two my second and probably largest annoyance with the book...the way in which Donati directs Hannah's story.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay, so I was not by any means at all a fan of the fact that Donati kills off Strikes-the-Sky <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It had taken me a bit to warm up to Strikes-the-Sky in Lake in the Clouds (honestly I had been holding out a secret hope that somehow Liam would change and his wife would be dead or something), but once I continued reading I perceived Strikes-the-Sky to be much better for Hannah/Walkes-Ahead because he sees both the Mahican and White parts of her. So there I am in my little blissful contentment after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a> that Strikes-the-Sky and Hannah are perfect and will live happily ever after, and then I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72856.Fire_Along_the_Sky__Wilderness___4_" title="Fire Along the Sky (Wilderness, #4) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire Along the Sky</a>. If I ever thought of not finishing the series in the middle of the series, it would have been when I found out-- after starting to read the book-- that Strikes-the-Sky has gone with Manny Freedman and Hannah presumes him dead. I was livid when I read this...for goodness sakes Donati had take Liam away from Hannah and now she takes Strikes-the-Sky away; I honestly think it was for more shock and awe affect than anything else--as in 'Let's see how far we can take Hannah's life and make it into the most wretched and difficult we can short of killing her'. Alright, maybe I'm a going over the top a little, but it really did anger me that Donati would put Strikes-the-Sky into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a> at the end to comfort us over the fact that Liam Kirby has turned out to not be Hannah's true love, and then not even bother to put him into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72856.Fire_Along_the_Sky__Wilderness___4_" title="Fire Along the Sky (Wilderness, #4) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire Along the Sky</a> except when he visits Hannah in her dreams. I honestly think it would have been better if she had never created his character and just had Hannah have a desire to head west with her uncle Otter. <br /><br />Okay, now onto the parts that I did like.<br /><br />I fell in LOVE with Lily and Simon! Yes, she seemed a little spoiled, but I couldn't help but watch as the two of them circled around each other. Him loving her and trying to show her that she loves and needs him too was one of the most beautiful tales of courtship to read about; they are perfect for each other! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Seriously loved when she threw the bottle of rose oil at him! It showed that she had guts and wasn't going to go down without a fight or giving her opinion.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, I liked Luke and Jennet. It was really the first time we are given a glimpse into Nathaniel Bonner's first child by Gisele Somerville, but he proves to be quite a interesting and dynamic character. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/820956.Dawn_on_a_Distant_Shore__Wilderness___2_" title="Dawn on a Distant Shore (Wilderness, #2) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Dawn on a Distant Shore</a>, I had loved Jennet's little character as she takes Hannah all through the nooks and cranies of the Earl's house in Scotland. In this book she becomes a character of depth and courage (a little idiotic for leaving the letters) but a natural heroine to join the rest. <br /><br />So final conclusion...I would have given this book 4 stars or even 4.5, but I just could not get over the jump in time because it wasn't well established in what happened during the 10 years between the two books and the way in which Donati directed Hannah's life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5661912140557002442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_85578558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85578558" />
    <a title="Jenny Q" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2661064-jenny-q"><img alt="Jenny Q" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257813597p2/2661064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85578558?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Q" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Q" href="/user/show/2661064-jenny-q">Jenny Q</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2661064-jenny-q?shelf=my-favorite-reads">my-favorite-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2661064-jenny-q?shelf=historical-fiction-faves">historical-fiction-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85578558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13026290964247925576">4.5 Stars. Ten years have passed since Hannah married Strikes-the-Sky and walked west with him to live among his people and now she is back in Paradise, alone, a quiet shell of her former self. She's not the only one who's found their way home to the welcoming arms of the Bonner family. Her newly widowed cousin from Scotland, Jennet, has arrived looking to rekindle her relationship with her first love, Hannah's half-brother Luke. Luke's home, too, and he's brought his business partner, fellow Sc</span>
  <span id="freeText13026290964247925576" style="display:none">4.5 Stars. Ten years have passed since Hannah married Strikes-the-Sky and walked west with him to live among his people and now she is back in Paradise, alone, a quiet shell of her former self. She's not the only one who's found their way home to the welcoming arms of the Bonner family. Her newly widowed cousin from Scotland, Jennet, has arrived looking to rekindle her relationship with her first love, Hannah's half-brother Luke. Luke's home, too, and he's brought his business partner, fellow Scot Simon Ballantyne, who has eyes only for Lily, the youngest Bonner daughter.<br /><br />Hannah was my favorite character in books two and three of this series, but Lily takes center stage for me in this novel as she struggles to make the transition from girl to woman. Lily's plans to study art in Europe have been foiled by the outbreak of the War of 1812, and her life is further complicated by an illicit relationship. Eighteen years old, headstrong and with a wild streak, Lily is determined to chart her own future, and she begins by convincing her parents to let her live and study art in Montreal with her brother Luke.<br /><br />Lily's twin, Daniel, also leaves Paradise with his cousin Blue Jay to join the war and soon finds himself taken prisoner. Lily and Simon make the dangerous trip through the battle lines to bring the news to Paradise, where the decision is made for Hannah and Jennet to set out with Luke's help to bring Daniel home.<br /><br />As war breaks out along the Canadian border, the narrative moves back and forth between Montreal, the battlefields, and Nathaniel and Elizabeth in Paradise, who in addition to worrying for their children, have problems of their own to face at home. This novel has a large cast of characters and there are multiple story threads, but even though they are separated, the Bonner family is never far from each other in thought and heart. The story concentrates on the younger generation, but Nathaniel and Elizabeth are still integral characters and the population of Paradise colorfully portrays the ups and downs of frontier life on the edge of the vast New York wilderness.<br /><br />I really like this series, I own all of them except the final book, which was recently published, but with this book as in the others, there are always a couple of things that nag at me and keep me from giving them five stars. Two in this one: First, It took me a long time to warm to Jennet; I found her annoying and callously happy to be a widow, though by her own admission her husband was a good man, even thought the marriage was arranged. And second, the story held on a little too long. With so many characters and plotlines, it took too long to bring it all together and the pace slowed down when I was ready to get to the end to see what the conclusion would be.<br /><br />In this book a few lingering loose ends from previous books are tied up, but several things are left hanging and the basis for the next book is presented, so I'm moving right on to Queen of Swords. Then I think I'll wait a while to read Endless Forests. I'm not quite ready to read the end of the story yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13026290964247925576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18166091151907982516">Took me a while to really get involved in this segment of the Bonner's story. I can't quite determine why as I've been eager to hear more about Jennet since she was first introduced. I was a bit upset that Hannah's story took such a sad turn after the bright childhood she had. I loved watching Lily & Simon fall for each other, and Luke and Jennet keep me happy as well. I wanted to know more about how Blue Jay suddenly came home with a wife having found her sometime after leaving the prisoner's s</span>
  <span id="freeText18166091151907982516" style="display:none">Took me a while to really get involved in this segment of the Bonner's story. I can't quite determine why as I've been eager to hear more about Jennet since she was first introduced. I was a bit upset that Hannah's story took such a sad turn after the bright childhood she had. I loved watching Lily &amp; Simon fall for each other, and Luke and Jennet keep me happy as well. I wanted to know more about how Blue Jay suddenly came home with a wife having found her sometime after leaving the prisoner's ship and making it back home. I've never felt like I knew Daniel well, and while his character grew a bit more toward the very end of this novel, I didn't feel like there was much to him beforehand to understand his strong emotions. The Stiler story seemed like a bit of interlude in the middle of the novel. I understand that it was a continuation of Jemima's mean-spirited tactics to hurt the people of Paradise, but it felt somewhat detached from everything else going on, and perhaps unnecessary since they were only run out of town a few chapters later anyway.<br /><br />Overall though, I do still love reading about this family and time period, and am very eager to see what happens with Luke &amp; Hannah's search for Jennet in the next segment.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_290665532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290665532" />
    <a title="Alexandria Brim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8071600-alexandria-brim"><img alt="Alexandria Brim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472974937p2/8071600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290665532?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandria Brim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandria Brim" href="/user/show/8071600-alexandria-brim">Alexandria Brim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8071600-alexandria-brim?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8071600-alexandria-brim?shelf=rhfl-challenge">rhfl-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8071600-alexandria-brim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8071600-alexandria-brim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8071600-alexandria-brim?shelf=american-history">american-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290665532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11781242372892486914">In her fourth book, nearly ten years have passed since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_' title='Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lake in the Clouds</a>. The War of 1812 has started and not even the residents of Hidden Wolf are spared. Lily, ready to go study art abroad, has her plans put on hold. Her brother Daniel and their cousin Blue Jay long to go fight. Elizabeth wishes to keep all her children on Hidden Wolf, safe. And into this walks Hannah, a shadow of her former self. The Bonners are also surprised by the arrival of Luke, Nathaniel's illegitimate son, and Jennet,</span>
  <span id="freeText11781242372892486914" style="display:none">In her fourth book, nearly ten years have passed since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a>. The War of 1812 has started and not even the residents of Hidden Wolf are spared. Lily, ready to go study art abroad, has her plans put on hold. Her brother Daniel and their cousin Blue Jay long to go fight. Elizabeth wishes to keep all her children on Hidden Wolf, safe. And into this walks Hannah, a shadow of her former self. The Bonners are also surprised by the arrival of Luke, Nathaniel's illegitimate son, and Jennet, a distant cousin from Scotland. <br /><br />Luke soon departs for Montreal, taking Daniel, Blue Jay and Lily with him. The boys join up with a military unit while Lily goes to study in the Canadian city. There she strikes up a relationship with Luke's friend Simon Ballentyne. <br /><br />The growing romance is quite sweet, though it heats up pretty quick. I was hesitant, I'll admit. After how much I disliked Hannah's romance in "Lake in the Clouds," I lost my trust in Donati a little to tell a romance that wasn't Elizabeth and Nathaniel. But I liked Simon and Lily's. Except for the sex. It's getting quite predictable. All major couples Donati pairs up have sex before they get married. Elizabeth and Nathaniel. Hannah and Strikes-the-Sky. Jennet and Luke. And now Lily and Simon. While I like Donati's sex scenes and find them organic to the story, I want to see a couple actually wait.<br /><br />Hannah's story is very interesting as well. And heartbreaking. I'll admit I wasn't too upset to find out Strikes-the-Sky was most likely dead. As I made clear in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a> review, I did not care for the romance. Hannah's loss of her child was heartbreaking as was the story surrounding it. While "Lake in the Clouds" was about Hannah becoming an adult, "Fire Along the Sky" is about her healing. <br /><br />But "Lake in the Clouds" was Hannah's story; "Fire Along the Sky" is mainly Lily's. She travels to Quebec to fulfill her dream of being artist. But it ultimately ends up being her romance. Lily has to choose between two suitors. Her first choice is Nicholas Wilde, a townsperson who owns an apple orchard. He is married though his wife has a form of dementia. Upon the return of Luke, Lily meets his friend and partner Simon Ballentyne. He is attracted to the woman and courts her in Quebec. Lily learns that Nicholas has married Jemima. She goes to Simon and agrees to marry him if he takes her home. <br /><br />The two then embark back for Paradise. As they ride through the Canadian wilderness, they run into soldiers. Nearly all of them know of her father, even the soldiers who capture Simon and interrogate Lily. In the process, she learns from her cousin that her brother has been captured. Lily, naturally, wants to help him but Simon and her cousin are against it. They believe the only person who can help Daniel is Hannah. Lily agrees to get her, though she feels useless. <br /><br />This time, Donati handles the multiple plots better than in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72855.Lake_in_the_Clouds__Wilderness___3_" title="Lake in the Clouds (Wilderness, #3) by Sara Donati" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake in the Clouds</a>. One chapter deals with Lily's story, the other focuses on the happenings in Paradise. And things are happening in Paradise--it's an episode of "Murder, She Wrote." And everyone suspects Jemima Southern Kuick Wilde, hoping to be rid of her for good. In the process, her daughter Martha and Nicholas' daughter Callie move in with Curiosity, who has inherited Richard Todd's house. They live there under the care of Jennet and Hannah as well--the entire town takes to caring for the girls in their parents' time of trouble. It's a sweet, if sad, plot. <br /><br />Once Lily arrives in Paradise, we have a flip-flop. Hannah and Jennet depart for Nut Island while Lily remains behind. The scenes of Nut Island are interesting with a mystery brewing. Hannah is back in her element as a doctor with Jennet serving as her assistant. The Scot has her own task as well. She uses her charms and diplomacy to navigate the officers in charge of the fort to help the prisoners. While doing so, she meets a Catholic priest that arouses her suspicions. Jennet pretends to be someone who he can convert in order to get close to him while Hannah tends to her injured brother. Daniel has a bullet inside him but his worst injury is to his arm. How he feels is hidden by the fact he's given laudanum and the fact that he's a boy. <br /><br />Not that's not to say that Donati ignores a character because of sex. It's just that most of her narrators are women. And as a woman author, I know it's easier to write a character the same sex as you. So Elizabeth, Hannah, Jennet and Lily are the ones who are telling this story. Occasionally, we get glimpses into Nathaniel's mind, but not often and only when Donati wishes to give the reader knowledge that is important but will be hidden from Elizabeth. So we will only see and experience Daniel's pain and how he copes through the eyes of his sisters and cousin. <br /><br />While I do like the romances in this book more--namely Jennet and Luke's as well as Lily and Simon's--a thought struck me as I was reading. Donati writes the same romance. Her female characters are all similar. They are fiery, passionate women who will not be told what to do. They will not be forced into the roles society demands of them. These are women with minds of their own and they will speak it. So their men need to be patient yet willing to love their plucky sides. And so they are: Nathaniel, Luke, Simon. Calm men who understand their women better than the women. Who have patience yet their own tempers to fight back. Whose passions run deep. The men know they love the women before the women do.* They just have the convince the women of the truth.**<br /><br />*Jennet is the exception. She pursues Luke and convinces him of their love. <br /><br />**I still hold that Hannah was just worn down and did not love Strikes-the-Sky at their wedding. But I will accept that she came to love him in the last ten years. <br /><br />I get that a modern woman may not necessarily like to read about demure girl who gets courted in the usual manner. We've come to expect our romantic heroines to be firecrackers, to espouse views that our more in line with ours. And it's not like there weren't fiery progressive women. But as both a reader and a writer, I believe it's quite boring to write essentially the same path each time. Yes, it is one that has proved successful. But variety is a good thing. <br /><br />There are side plots to the romance. After Dolly Wilder's death and Nicholas' marriage to Jemima, things get worse for the man. She sells his land to a minister, who arrives in Paradise to find a cold reception. First is because Nicholas surrenders his land to the man without a fight before disappearing into the brush. Then his message isn't too welcomed by the people who have kept their religion (mostly) to themselves. He butts heads with Elizabeth over her decision to educate girls and blacks in her school. The man comes very close to slut shaming Lily over the fact that everyone in the village knows she's already having sex with Simon. This is presented as him being wrong, when in a lot of ways, he's right. Most preachers would be against this practice, though maybe a more sympathetic preacher would address the couple in private. It was hard to dislike the man in this circumstance because I felt it wouldn't kill the two to not be so obvious. Especially after the town was certain she was committing adultery with Nicholas Wilde. I may be making too much of it, but it was clear that Donati expected us to feel angry for Lily's sake and I just couldn't. <br /><br />In the end, the Reverend Stiles proves to be a brief foe as his preaching backfires <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when his own nephew attempts to rape Lily, believing his uncle that she's a whore. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The Bonners go back to being happy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(even for a near attempt, Lily bounces back very quickly) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and Callie gets her house back. <br /><br />At the fort, Liam Kirby returns. I'm not spoilering it because even I spent the entire book waiting for it. He is reunited with Hannah and learns about his daughter, Martha. We get the closest to romance between him and Hannah but some resolution. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He dies at Nut Island. If you followed my status updates, you know I felt guilty for wishing him to do so. Donati went a bit overboard in my opinion to assure us that Liam was going to die and not reunite with Hannah. Beyond a miraculous recovery, this was overkill. Showing his decline and then revealing his death would've been enough for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />These were only a few complaints in a story that otherwise kept me riveted. If you liked Donati's other novels, I definitely recommend them. If you haven't read her other books, I advise you to start with "Into the Wilderness." There are callbacks to events and characters from her previous books that will be difficult to understand without reading them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11781242372892486914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2526144058558296003" style="display:none">Rating: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ 1/2<br />•<br />Book 4 of Sara Donati’s Wilderness series follows Hannah as she struggles to recover from heartache, Jennet as she follows her heart to the endless forests, and Lily as she tries to carve a life for herself as an artist. To complicate things, there’s a war on, and the Bonner family once again finds themselves in the midst of it all.<br />•<br />One thing I love about this series – while there’s lots of action and big plot points, it’s Donati’s world building and descriptions of daily life during this time period that really set the tone for the book. <br />•<br />Six Things I Loved About Fire Along the Sky:<br /><br />1.	This book is what started my brief love of tarot cards. Jennet learns to read the cards while travelling from Scotland to Canada. I have a gorgeous set of cards, but never learned to read them.<br /><br />2.	Richard Todd CARES! His heart isn’t as black as he lets people think it is. I loved the reading of his will. He knows just what everyone needs to be able to carry on.<br /><br />3.	Loved how Jennet fits seamlessly into Paradise.<br /><br />4.	The care packages the Bonner family send to those who are far away. We’re currently living in a different country than all our family, and care packages are so wonderful to receive. I can imagine the thought and love the Bonners put into each letter and package they send to Hannah, Jennet, and the boys.<br /><br />5.	Liam and Hannah reuniting, however briefly.<br /><br />6.	Each book just brings me to tears. The love in this family is so overwhelming.<br />•<br />Donati’s writing is as always superb. She blends history and fiction seamlessly.</span>

But mourning the loss of both husband and child, she is a shadow of a girl they once knew. Nonetheless, she resumes her medical duties in the village of Paradise, just as her cousin Jennet is reunited with Luke Bonner.   <span id="freeText16642578993673733149" style="display:none">Rating 3.5 <br /><br />The year is 1812, and Nathaniel's daughter, Hannah, has returned to Elizabeth and Nathaniel Bonner. But mourning the loss of both husband and child, she is a shadow of a girl they once knew. Nonetheless, she resumes her medical duties in the village of Paradise, just as her cousin Jennet is reunited with Luke Bonner. But the war with the British is escalating, and Luke leaves to fight, as does eighteen-year-old Lily Bonner's twin brother Daniel. Lily makes a decision that sends her to Montreal and into the arms of a most unusual man - who could love her properly, if only she would let him. With so many loved ones away and in danger, Nathaniel and Elizabeth must draw strength from each other and those remaining at Lake in the Clouds. <br /><br />This seems to be a transition book that tells the stories of Lily, Hannah and Jennet but leaves them with many unresolved issues. I'm hoping that the position of each of these ladies will be more clear in the following two books. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4184068644979833821">This is the 4th book in the series about the frontier family of Daniel & Elizabeth Bonner. I love this family and the characters in the book. I love the narrator of the audio version with her variety of voices from British Elizabeth to Scottish Jennet. She has lost her husband & son & has returned to Paradise only to be caught up in the War of 1812. Her brother Daniel has been </span>
  <span id="freeText4184068644979833821" style="display:none">This is the 4th book in the series about the frontier family of Daniel &amp; Elizabeth Bonner. I love this family and the characters in the book. I love the narrator of the audio version with her variety of voices from British Elizabeth to Scottish Jennet. Hannah of course is the strongest character with her indian &amp; white mixed heritage and the racial attitudes toward her. She has lost her husband &amp; son &amp; has returned to Paradise only to be caught up in the War of 1812. Her brother Daniel has been hurt &amp; taken prisoner so she ends up at the prisoner stockade taking care of him &amp; others. Jennet is with her and I find this to be the most interesting part of the book. These books are long so we must endure the day to day activities of Paradise which are important to the story. These are my kind of books and I will be sad when I read the last one. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2825978117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11890287519609797594">I continue to really enjoy this series, which chronicles the Bonner family's adventures. This novel focuses more on the Bonner children: Hannah, who has returned to Paradise and Lake in the Clouds as a bit of a broken woman; Luke, who has moved back to Montreal from Scotland; Jennet, the cousin we haven't seen much of since she was a young girl at the Carryck estate in Scotland; and Lily and Daniel, who are no longer children and are on the cusp of adulthood. Plenty of tense moments, as always, </span>
  <span id="freeText11890287519609797594" style="display:none">I continue to really enjoy this series, which chronicles the Bonner family's adventures. This novel focuses more on the Bonner children: Hannah, who has returned to Paradise and Lake in the Clouds as a bit of a broken woman; Luke, who has moved back to Montreal from Scotland; Jennet, the cousin we haven't seen much of since she was a young girl at the Carryck estate in Scotland; and Lily and Daniel, who are no longer children and are on the cusp of adulthood. Plenty of tense moments, as always, but I love the way Sara Donati allows her characters to grow and change, shaped by the events happening around them. This book felt more open-ended to me than the previous installments, so I will be reading book 5 very soon.....</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c5PW7o4Kjlu7waa+bxeZO6RFJIeXxWTB1atVFN14jgsK3M9ZRaT37zvLnQfIdkxJCMx1CmNb71vEuDSJgr8QwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('twIKX7/IW6UTePXIrDdyLdJhgp5RKnzz1N9HkVGhWcnOTRPodGYiEZNyznELVqdffujTE6W092nFzCYMDmbHAw==')})
  }

If anything, Matthew\'s insistence that he is an innocent man leads him to being singled out for the heaviest tasks. Insufficient food, gruelling days and the humid heat combine to wear him down. With a sinking feeling, he realises no one has ever survived their seven years of service on the plantation Suffolk Rose. Fortunately for Matthew, he has a remarkable wife. Alex  Graham has no intention of letting her husband suffer and die. So she sets off from Scotland on a perilous journey to bring her husband home. Alex is plagued by nightmares in which Matthew is reduced to a wheezing wreck by his tormentors. Sailing to Virginia, she prays for a miracle to carry her swiftly to his side. But fate has other plans, and what should have been a two month crossing turns into a year long adventure - from one side of the Atlantic to the other. Will Alex find Matthew in time? Will she be able to pay the price of setting him free? Like Chaff in the Wind continues on from The Rip in the Veil, taking Alex and Matthew\'s love story to a new continent.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12568976494775993611\" href=\"#\" Has Jemima come to claim her daughter–or does she have something else in mind? Whatever happens, Martha and Daniel and all the Bonners must stand united against the threats to both heart and home.Painful secrets and hidden sorrows, joy, heartbreak, and passion follow the Bonners through a season of change and renewal.
